when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式設計師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的事是:未來會比這更多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 一百年後 , 這個傢伙在1936年 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器都是機械 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turs機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都來自數學觀點 , 但追求告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把數學基金的數學基金給電腦科學 , 他說: 「 不管你如何製造電腦科學 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你是電腦的機械 , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage , 或電子 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得微小 。 這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 有一種計算能力 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你得到了這個連結 , 你把這個連結連結起來 , 就是電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以用電腦做一切 , 只有慢慢地 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡片 , 它會用punch卡ds , 它會被用來
it did have a ram pack .	牠有一隻強暴龍蝦 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上更多的記憶 , 如果你想要的話 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在劍魚 , 科學博物館 , 有數百種計劃和數百種計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝所寫的 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計畫 」 的計畫 , 我們計畫要建立一個差異的計畫 , 創造出不同的引擎 , 我們計畫要創造出不同的引擎 , 也是我們所謂的 「 計畫 」 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會創造出分析的引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計畫有幾部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中之一是關於babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 現在 , 目前正在研究所有這些計畫的研究 , 試圖決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是電腦模擬機器 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston , 理查德•雷斯頓的研究中 , 理查•雷斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓 , 理查•李安斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓 , 理查•雷斯頓 ,
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•安德森:歡迎到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體 , 左邊 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	底底是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩種大型x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 ; 男性x染色體 ;
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一個小小的東西讓你不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你可以看到 , 當然 , 這是這個基因組的組合 , 其中有四種生物化學信件 , 我們稱它們為基礎 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	在人類基因組中有多少人基因組 ? 30億 。

bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們把這個小型的小型需要 , 你知道 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們所做的是基本上 , 透過軟組織組織 , 把它們放在一起 , 將它變成硬骨頭骨髓 , 每次一次 , 一次 , 一個軟組織 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到海岸 , 把牠帶到海岸 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	回到我身上 , 我們再次再次做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手臂上 , 手臂的尾聲是 , 牠的頭髮看起來像瑞士一樣 , 像瑞士一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序已經改變了40年 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以 , 我認為最主要的新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 火箭礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	標準的標準 , 它的運作方式是這樣 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們標準的病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	而不是進入前面的前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個很棒的電池 , 用一個特殊的線路線圈圈圈圈圈 , 繞著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 很快地 , 你能迅速地啟動 , 或很快地發現 , 骨髓液體非常迅速 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以做多次通過相同的動作 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	很快地 , 鮑勃只能得到一個指令 , 包含了 , 讓它成為一個專家 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩著這一點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 很驚訝的是 , 我們不只能得到骨髓 , 我們也得到了10次的幹細胞活動 , 和一般裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置只是fda應用在過去一年 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡有一個活病患者 , 你可以看到它追蹤了極佳的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩位病患 , 相同的病人 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉劑中所做的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	再次 , 我們得到了三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比標準治療方法還要多 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是個非常豐富的成年幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成年人幹細胞在我們的骨髓裡培養幹細胞 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡包含血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 我們已經使用了一種形式的幹細胞 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 許多骨髓幹細胞可以治療病人的疾病 , 像是心臟病、肺結核病、肺結核病 , 及糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛進步 , 今年 , 世代2.0.0.0.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是 , 它會變得更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人來參加會議會鼓勵更多人 , 來成為潛能的生存者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可以讓你能在未來應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們骨髓移植手術的照片 , 每年在史丹佛大學 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這科技能讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和surfergarretttttttttttttlisi現在是最美麗的宇宙的新模型 , 它是你所見過最美麗的一系列圖形 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	格雷特•萊特斯在他的理論上找到了所有東西 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	那些殺人的法案 , 查出那些殺人的方案 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	為了接下來18分鐘我要做最好的我能描述美麗的美粒物理不平等
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚中學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭都有數千個單位的珊瑚 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些池子會不斷地擴散到基因上 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這個成為一個非常聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就可以獨立一個人 , 問他一個可理性的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他如何在這個特定的位置 , 和鄰居的鄰居比較近 , 只能問他是哪裡 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	為了讓溫度太高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你可以看到 , 我有很大的壓力 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個警察會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常清楚地描述他的鄰居 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在所有其他地方 , 但 , 把它們分離成分別 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分裂成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個很聰明的珊瑚會獨特地準備了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常精確描述宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對人類來說 , 很奇怪 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪 , 是他貓的第一次描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 一個叫做 「 量子力學 」 的理論 , 在這個組合中 , 用一種放射性來源 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本中 , 牠會把毒素和schrardinger死掉 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的領域中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些實體都是透過每個人體驗的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	如同所知 , 另一個人並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為每個人都只經歷一個獨立的存在 , 我們也不會看到其他的 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	像我們一樣 , 像schrodschrodschr , 是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這是世界如何運作 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子中出現:一切都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是關於描述可能發生什麼事 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都來自於幾何和相互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只要這些互動都是完美的平衡 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來講述我們如何了解這些粒子 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個叫做 「 原子 」 的 「 光 」 和 「 光 」 和 「 光 」 和 「 光線 」 和 「 光線 」 的聚集在一起 , 形成了一種爆炸的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這個能量會被轉換成一系列的物理粒子 , 偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這種巨大的機器巨大的機器大型工程是19英里的機器 , 當時是一間大型的石頭工程 , 每次當它運作時 , 畫出五倍的電力 , 將五倍的能量轉化為城市 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何個體內產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子如何產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有許多質量和能量 , 由質量和能量來組成 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子都比這個能量限制還沒那麼大 , 還能維持我們 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器很興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量限制七倍 , 這樣我們才能看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談談之前 , 讓我描述我們所知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個zo的物理粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡有許多人在這個房間裡有好活的推動 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	電荷和一個非常微小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 大大的質子和中子在原子中形成了質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左邊和右邊 , 和右邊有相反的粒子 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較少熟悉第二代和第三代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代和第三代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和各種力量粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電磁力互相作用 , 稱為光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一個非常弱的力量 , 一個非常弱的力量 , 一個非常弱的力量 , 一個非常弱的力量 , 一個非常弱的力量 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	強強的力量在三種不同的不同種類之間:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪怪的名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量是重力的力量 , 它會與物質維持關係 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解的是 , 這裡有不同的連結 , 和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這些四種不同的力量互相作用 , 每個粒子都有 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個粒子還沒見過 , 但我們很確定存在 , 希格斯粒子是希格斯粒子 , 它會給所有其他粒子 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型鐵柱的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要展示給大家看一段美好的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把所有這些不同的粒子使用不同的粒子 , 就會有2226 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	許多粒子可以持續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	它似乎很奇怪 , 自然會有很多元素 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們帶到他們的荷蘭 , 有些美麗的模式就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 電荷是三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和夸克結合在一起 , 它就會有一個電荷 , 它有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有相反的粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	現在 , 電荷是由兩個其他的組合組合起來: 「 電荷 」 和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	若我們把這些粒子放在兩維空間中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向上 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁和弱力互相作用 , 它會產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 獨立 」 的模式 , 它在1967年開始 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部分的人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊有巨大的質量並破壞對稱的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它會造成弱勢力弱的弱勢力很弱 , 使弱力非常弱力 , 使我們弱力弱力弱力 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為這張圖片中 , 電磁共振動脈 , 讓電磁力和電荷相互相互作用 , 讓電荷分裂在這個圖片中 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁和弱力被稱為二維空間的空間 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以包含強力的力量 , 將它們的兩載載荷 , 將它們的力量分散出來 , 將它們的力量分裂成兩載荷 , 引起強力的力量 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有知識粒子都可以在四維空間中旋轉 , 只能看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子互動時 , 自然保持在完美的平衡上 , 大自然會持續在完美的平衡中 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和抗粒子 , 它會創造出一個能量和一個抗粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和一個抗粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和抗粒子 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以製造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量和維持體內 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的抗粒子可以形成在一個撞擊中 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 荷爾斯必須要平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以拆解成電子和一顆粒子 , 而這些三則仍然加入了電子和一個細菌 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些圖案的模式並不只如此 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動發生了什麼事 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以把這三維空間帶到四維空間中 , 讓更好的視力互相對稱 , 讓更好的視力互相對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強強的力量粒子中 , 例如這個綠色 , 一個強強的力量粒子 , 例如這個綠色 , 一個強強的力量粒子 , 例如這個綠色 , 讓夸克和顏色混合在一起 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動會發生數百萬次 , 在我們的身體中 , 將原子核融合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四條曲線對三種力量來說是不是故事的 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種更重力的力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們包含這些 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都在六維空間中建立一個很好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看它很不錯 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們最好的知識大自然所建構在小規模的範圍內 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是非常限制的 , 我們能夠和實驗進行實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和古老的想法我們不知道
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式 , 用數學 , 看看我們是否能得到我們的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 讓宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這個圖片來預測新粒子 , 我們想要用這個圖片來預測新的粒子 , 我們想要用這張圖來預測新的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子中有個古老的概念 , 叫做 「 粒子 」 的概念 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 來產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新力量 , 以新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新方向時 , 我們猜測量粒子在哪裡移動 , 然後我們就可以與他人溝通 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜測量 , 我們就能建構標準室內的三維空間 , 以七維空間的形狀呈現 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特定的選擇在1973年被巴蒂和薩爾斯坦所提到 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新模式時 , 我們可以看到 , 有些粒子似乎失敗了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是科學研究的理論 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家看起來更大、更大、更大、更大、更有形狀的模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測原始存在的存在粒子從未見過 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個預測存在於這些兩種新力量的存在 , 它應該像弱勢力 , 只有弱勢力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以把這組合成七維空間 , 以七維空間為第一代 , 並考慮一個奇怪的事實 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地辨識出6個載荷 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準室的旁邊 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八維空間中運作 , 那麼我們可以為每個粒子創造出獨特的新荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以用八度維度 , 看看整個模式的樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一代相對稱作 「 三世代 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八維空間中 , 它是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大型的圖案之一 , 第八個 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言是平均的248度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	每個角度都對應對對稱的對稱性非常複雜、美麗 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	其中一個小小的部分 , 可以用來描述南斯坦的二氧化碳 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 幾何形狀可以描述宇宙如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這個形狀在八維空間中有數千種可能的交互作用 , 它總結成千上萬種可能的互動 , 這種形狀的形狀是非常美麗的 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過這個圖案 , 我們可以透過這個圖案 , 看到所有粒子 , 看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 我們可以看到一些洞見到新粒子被這個模式所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個粒子 , 兩種都被稱為 「 粒子 」 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個模式中 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子 , 但有顏色和強力 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新粒子中 , 把這些新粒子變成了這個模式 , 給了我們全全的8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這八種模式有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的數學美麗可以描述真相對於粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然的概念是 , 大自然被數學並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這篇文章: 「 大自然的本書 」 大自然的本書 , 它不斷地開放到我們的 「 大自然 」 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	角色是三角形、圓形、圓圈和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有這些 , 每個人都無法理解一個單字 , 不論是在黑暗實驗室中 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是正確的 , 我相信這句話是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的數學粒子物理用三角形、圓圈和其他幾何形狀 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 身為物理學家 , 我真的在研究這些東西 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的實驗室 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的數學是純粹、美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學有關 , 這個數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 和量子力學有關 , 這個數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 和量子力學 , 這個數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 和量子力學有關 , 這個數學描述了我們宇宙的成長 , 直到一個美麗的形狀 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式 , 我們可能可以看到自然是否使用新機器 , 像是大型鐵行器 , 我們可能可以看到自然是否使用新機器 , 像是大型鐵行器 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現是很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到粒子 , 它會很酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新粒子 , 但它們並不符合這種模式 , 這種模式很有趣 , 但它們並不符合這種模式 , 很有趣 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說 , 對我來說很糟 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會怎麼樣 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的工作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的東西是長期的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	大部分的研究都知道大部分這些想法可能不會終於大自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論 , 像是:有很多線索 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論就像創創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有任何大型投資 , 可以讓人難以置信 , 很難避免疫情 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果你沒有工作 , 你必須去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 唯一能維持幸福的方式 , 就是保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我曾嘗試過最好的辦法 , 能活得更好 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我人生的平衡 , 和我自己的三條路徑 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣 , 即使我所研究的物理 , 我仍然知道我已經活過了好生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去幾十年來 , 我住在土地 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是宇宙中最偉大的神秘之一 , 是我的父母 , 我如何管理生存 , 沒有參與任何合適的空間 , 才能存活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要讓各位放入這個秘密 。

but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他認為 , 很常見的理論是 , 如果我們找到行為模式 , 或同一個共同的理論 , 如果我們找到行為模式 , 或相同在我們最親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近親近活
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老、古老的歷史上學到了這些特質 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今的教科書 , 人類進化 , 你通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們也聽過這個ted會議 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 為了我來評論這些黑猩猩的行為 , 我們對牠們的行為有多樣性 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 , 儘管我們認為大多數人可能不會在260歲以後才有60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	mr.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel.wurzel
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	每五年或六年 , 孩子在晚上睡覺 , 媽媽在晚上醒來 , 把她帶回來 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 我們很長期對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 因為我們和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦變得更加複雜 , 我們發現學習玩耍更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察牠們的生長 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道 , 牠們有能力模仿行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這樣我們就可以描述這些工具的行為 , 以這種方式來描述這些行為 , 如原始文化一樣 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩不會有語言 , 我們已經談過 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們有很豐富的能力 , 許多類似的東西 , 或甚至身分辨識出相同的情況 , 或甚至身分辨識出相似 , 或甚至身分辨識出來的人 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也kis , 雙手 , 握手 , 把手放在一起 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們會搖搖搖滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們找到許多的例子 , 包括同情心 , 愛和真實的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們就像我們一樣 , 牠們的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們是非常殘酷的 , 甚至是極端的殘酷 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常強烈的行為 , 大部分的部分 , 都被剝奪到鄰居社會群體的行為 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常精彩的動作 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有鯊魚 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	它是非常模糊的 , 而且它變得越來越模糊了 , 隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究 , 當時仍持續持續 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 在野生動物中 , 牠們的複雜社群生活在野生中 , 和我們分享地球的動物有多大 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很讓人驚訝的是 , 牠們棲息地在世界各地尋找黑猩猩 , 像其他生物一樣 , 牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這張照片是從空氣中拍攝的 , 它讓大家看到森林的高島 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	當時我在1960年 , 發現在公園裡 , 在1960年以前 , 幾乎沒辦法在公園裡出現 , 當時我在公園的森林裡 , 發現在公園裡 , 這裡有三十四個國家公園 , 在1960年 , 幾乎沒辦法破裂 , 當時在公園的森林中 , 那裡有三十四個國家公園 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何嘗試拯救這些美麗的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園時 , 他們會怎麼做 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多的人居住在土地上 , 無法支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量增加了 , 來自布朗克斯的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	很窮的人他們無法負擔得起買食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常可愛的生活方式 , 讓人們住在公園裡的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始小 , 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去探險 , 但它包含了一些像是樹木護士 , 幾乎沙漠的土地在這些山脈中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制方式 , 避免土壤 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建農島的兩年之內 , 牠們可以再次做生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民們獲取水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造了一些學校
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小組婦女合作 , 提供他們機會 , 給微貸貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們已經發現了 , 全球大約95%的貸款都退休了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 她們可以完成第二課學校 , 很明顯了解 , 全世界各地 , 女性教育 , 提供獎學金 , 她們可以完成第二課的教育 , 讓女性教育改善 , 家庭大小 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供資訊有關家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	結果是為了保育 , 事情發生了 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的重點是 , 農夫住在24村的村莊裡 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 農夫住在這24村的村莊裡 , 但當我們開始教職計畫時 , 農夫住在這24村的村莊裡 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	這是坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民說話 , 問他們對他們有什麼興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 開始改善 , 他們開始改善 , 開始改善 ,
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 如山丘的大樓層面積木 , 所以你有了這種可怕的土壤和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展出我們所謂的 「 更大規模的發展 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園的地面 , 把它們放大到全國公園 , 延伸到全國公園 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村莊有更好的標準 , 他們的確認同步在公園中有一百五十個國家公園 , 一旦這些村莊有更好的標準 , 牠們會有更好的標準 , 牠們會在公園裡有更好的標準 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲各地的其他地方 , 其他的地區 , 都在非洲的另一邊 , 還有其他的地區 , 也有極大的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲 , 我們已經討論過這個問題 , 大部分的問題都是 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很多貧窮的問題 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你砍下樹木時 , 會發生什麼事 ? 要給予任何東西 , 讓它們能在土地上生存下來 , 讓它們能為自己和家人存活 , 特別是在你砍下樹木時 , 會發生什麼事 ? 要怎麼做 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	還有其他問題 , 不只非洲 , 而是其他的問題 , 包括我們在地球上所做的事 。
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 科學家 , 歐.威爾遜說 , 如果每個人在這個星球上擁有三個新星球 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們會說四個 。 但我們沒有他們 , 我們有了 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我是說 , 在這裡 , 我們是最有智慧的 , 人類是地球上最有智慧的 , 它是地球上最有智慧的 , 最有智慧的能力 , 可以透過這些ted會議 , 來到這裡 , 我們有著最聰明的能力 , 可以透過這些ted會議 , 並且我們還能被這些ted會議所展示出來 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的人 , 在他們做了一個重大決策之前 , 問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們人類七代前的遺產 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 大部分的決定 , 我不是特別談論非洲 , 而是發展出世界主要決策 , 數百萬人 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 會如何影響下一個共鳴 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地討論這個問題時 , 我了解到很多非洲的問題 , 都能在非洲各地開始旅行 , 我了解到更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 都能被黑猩猩和其餘生存活下來 , 我了解到更多 , 很多非洲的問題都能被黑猩猩及其餘生存活下來 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始旅行非洲 , 談到歐洲 , 談到美國 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都是這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們知道我在談論污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣 , 通常會吸毒我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在污染我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水可能是最關鍵的問題之一 , 我們要面對這個世紀、工業和家庭的化學物質 , 都可以從過去經驗中獲益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	海嘯的效果變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們討論了土壤 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無可避免的燃料 , 和其他溫室氣體排放 , 所以稱之為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都相信 , 我們的氣候變遷很有趣 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合起來 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會被影響更糟 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經被影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季發生時 , 通常會導致災難、飢餓、飢餓、飢餓和疾病 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個地區的人口數量 , 都無法逃離 , 因為整個土地都被降低了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會被切割 , 分裂 , 回到樹木的最後一棵樹 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這不只在非洲 , 而是世界各地 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 讓我感到驚訝的是 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去智慧 , 智慧的智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你覺得可能有一些差異嗎 ? 與同情心有關嗎 ? 與同情心有關嗎 ? 人類的腦袋 , 與同情心有關嗎 ? 和同情心有關嗎 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們說了 「 不論 」 、 「 感覺 」 、 「 我們感覺 」 , 因為我們感覺到他們 , 基本上就是他們說 「 不 」 、 「 種族 」 、 「 種族 」 、 「 我們感受到他們 」 , 基本上就是他們對他們說 「 種族 」 、 「 種族 」 。
we have compromised their future .	我們已經對他們的未來感到沮喪 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三隻小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我感覺到這個美麗的星球 , 每當我看它們時 , 我就會感受到這個美麗的星球 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這引起了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 羅根和槍擊 」 , 開始在坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經傳播到全球各國各地 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射光看起來很小 ; 到太陽能破壞牆壁 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	看看布里克牆 , 所有這些問題都在地球上 , 環境和社會 , 這是希望的未來 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數以千計的年輕人 , 可以破解 , 可以破壞 , 可以破壞 , 讓這個世界更好的生活 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	最重要的訊息之一:每個人每天都有不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 , 每個人在這個房間裡 , 我們都有選擇 , 每個人在這個房間裡 , 我們都有選擇 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的選擇 , 沒有選擇 , 而是我們要改變事物 , 貧窮的選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	樹根和芽團體都有三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它依賴於他們在城市或鄉村地區 , 不管他們是城市或鄉村 , 還是鄉村 。

artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家diannacohen分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真相 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 我們的生活中有一些關於塑膠污染的真相 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	安娜•柯林:對塑膠污染的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中一位視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中之一 , 塑膠污染聯盟 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋子一起工作 , 我把它切割成兩年後的原始材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩、三維、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	過去八年來 , 我的工作開始分裂 , 有點塑膠的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	更進一步 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠碎片變成小小點子 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中 , 許多人都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 學到了關於太平洋垃圾和葡萄酒 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是: 「 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須走出去 , 去清理它 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我發現了一個建議 , 一個結合 , 一台機器 , 和一台機器 , 一個很棒的機器 , 和一個很棒的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意見是 , 開始把塑膠放進去 , 把塑膠放進去 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 , 把塑膠放在一起 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和人們談談 , 實際上 , 我開始和大家談談 , 實際上我需要回去看更大的圖片 , 看看更大的圖片 , 看看更大的圖片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的重點是:我們需要找到一種方法來轉移 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷這些塑膠 , 進入海洋環境 , 每天都在全球規模上 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 我也了解到 , 我也意識到我很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只擔心塑膠 , 可能是塑膠 , 在五大海洋中 , 我已經知道現在有11種塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是塑膠的塑膠 , 我很擔心它是塑膠的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠中 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的平均都包裝在塑膠中 , 甚至在健康食物市場上 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我很擔心塑膠和毒素從塑膠中吸收到我們的身體 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以 , 我和一群人一起研究這問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果80到90%我們在海洋中找到的海洋是塑膠 , 為什麼我們不稱它為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人 , 回收這些書 , 讓所有人都能永續發展 , 重新循環 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進去 , 不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 不到7%的塑膠都是回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細看 , 特別是當它進入塑膠瓶子時 , 大部分都只有下降 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被用在塑膠瓶裡 , 再一次塑膠瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶 , 再一次塑膠瓶子再一次塑膠瓶子 。
so this is a big issue for us .	對我們來說 , 這是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件事我們正在找尋求大家思考: 「 重新回收 」 、 「 回收 」 、 「 回收 」 、 「 回收 」 、 「 回收 」 、 「 回收 」 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	除非可見的塑膠 , 無法塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是很古老的
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在收集了這些酷色的玩具 , 把食物放進去儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人做一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易挑出一座鋼瓶 , 或玻璃瓶 , 把你的鋼瓶放到水裡 , 或水面上 , 再加上水 , 或玻璃瓶 , 把你的儲存石瓶裝滿水 , 或玻璃瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想告訴大家 , 我知道你們知道你們知道大家知道很多關於這問題的問題是 , 這是一個巨大的問題 , 但這是我們所創造的一個大問題 , 是我們所創造的 , 可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個議題 , 教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 若要選擇替代方案 , 就可以選擇替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們能拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們的地球 。

i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我曾很感興趣 , 我們能否演化或發展出一個六感 , 來幫助我們做出正確的決策 , 不論我們是否能否演化或資訊 , 可能存在某些地方 , 來幫助我們做出正確的決策 。

so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們不太容易取得所有相關資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 才能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 才能協助我們做出最佳決定 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我的研究團隊在媒體實驗室研發了一系列的發明 , 來讓我們取得這些資訊 , 很容易的方法 , 不用說 , 使用者改變自己的行為 。

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里斯和安德里斯•羅德里德里斯和安德里斯•羅德里斯和安達•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德里斯•羅德瑞茲在2001年9月11 , 2001年9月11 , 2001年9月11日 , 這兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都能找到和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都能找到和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都能找到和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來找和平 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治 。

we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否已經活到36小時後 。

and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後 , 美國政府稱之為死刑 , 對他來說 , 如果被告知 , 我丈夫和我的同事 , 會被告知 , 和美國政府稱之為死刑 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過人類權利團體 , 我們和其他受害者的家庭合作 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在19世紀末期 , 詩人寫了一首詩 。

and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是我們現在看到的 , 很明顯的 , 通常都是非常嚴重的時刻 , 通常都是很明顯的 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 它會發生在每一世紀 。

and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在美國的戰爭中 , 兩次大戰後 , 世界大戰發生了兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	馬西歐文戰爭 , 可能更準確地描述它們 。

we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到一些不同的東西 , 在歐洲文明中 , 我們看到了一些不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不僅僅是來自國內的國家 。

what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今 , 國內的權力已經遷移到全球階層 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談論全球化的全球化 , 但實際上它是全球化的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國際舞台上 , 國際舞台也不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和國際舞台 , 國際舞台和全球階層的力量 , 國際舞台和全球階層的力量 , 如今 , 國際舞台和全球階層的力量 , 可以讓國際舞台和全球階梯的力量 , 像是金融交易 , 供應付出金融交易的力量 , 最終 , 國際舞台和全球階層的力量 , 比數量更大的數量還要大 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球空間中 , 沒有被規定法律的規律 , 而人們可能會自由地做法律 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 要強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	它總是適合在空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間空間不只由於你想要國際貿易、交易、網路、網路等等 , 而是你所想要的國際貿易、網路、等等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的事件是 , 即使你是地球上最偉大的國家 , 甚至是地球上最有力的國家之一 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是地球上最有力的國家 , 即使你是世界上最有力的國家 ,
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	這樣說 , 大約60%的40000萬美元被送到9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你可以看到 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間 , 太空旅行 , 網絡 , 衛星廣播 , 可以用這個空間 , 來到那裡的太空 , 和我們的系統和我們的方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久後 , 歷史的規則 , 歷史的規則就是權力管理必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信 , 這是我們時間的關鍵之一 , 就是把全球化的力量帶進去 , 全球化的力量也是如此 。

now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有問題 , 我們就會回來 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合起來 , 把最強大的規則 , 把最強大的力量 , 把最強大的制度放在一起 , 把最強大的制度放在一起 , 把最強大的制度放在一起 , 來解決解決方案 , 那麼 , 會發生什麼事 ?

so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 是我的第一條信息是 , 若你要通過這些推動 , 不管是如何 , 我們的成功 , 會在大量依賴我們的能力上 , 才能讓全球空間變得更不穩定 。

my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟聽眾談談這個議題 , 但權力不只是轉變 , 還要轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說故事 , 文明的歷史 , 文明的歷史 , 文明已經被文明化的歷史文明化了 , 在西方國家的歷史中 , 文明已經被文明化的歷史文明已經被文明化了 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到了一種基本的轉變 , 從國家聚集在一起 , 來到國會聚集在大西洋岸邊 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	現在從經濟力量開始 , 但那就是一直開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 在世界各地的發展中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為事實上這不是從西方到東邊的轉移 , 有些事情發生了 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜猜是 , 美國將會保持世界上最強大的國家 , 美國將會保持在世界上最強大的國家 , 在接下來10年 , 十五歲 , 但她所能做的 , 是 , 最強大的國家在未來十年內 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們花了50年的時間 , 歷史上最不尋常的 , 在我們所擁有的最不尋常的情況下 , 世界上最不尋常的時刻 , 每一組合理 , 都可以被它所謂的 「 地球 」 所包容 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是常常的案例
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現今的新興是歷史上最常見的情況 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你剛剛開始看到世界的流動性 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國已經成為我們世界最主要的特徵 。

europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在19世紀:一個偉大的英國外國秘密 , 叫做 「 歐洲人權力 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 五維的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是扮演著平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎與柏林合作 , 英國和羅馬合作 , 來提供一個不平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在 , 注意到 , 在一個日期內 , 全球各地都有固定的維護人 , 被稱為 「 獨裁者 」 , 全國都被打破了 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	權力的權力意味著修復 。

and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們所處的世界 , 我們會發現我們的盟友並不是固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	英國外科曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的利益 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會發現 , 儘管我們在西方國家中 , 我們會發現 , 若我們想要在世界各地 , 到達出去 , 我們就會發現 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	這樣說 , 當我們進入libya時 , 它不夠好 , 我們必須把其他人帶進去 。

my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜是 , 我們到了四百年後 , 四百年來 , 我說400年了 , 因為它是西方國家的西方力量、西方國家、西方國家的力量、西方力量、西方國家 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 若西方世界各地的角落 , 就能提出和歧視 。

today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 我們現代世界的原因是 , 所有東西都與一切有關聯繫 。

the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家的國際關係 , 它總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外國是關於國際關係的聯繫 。
